title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Poole" title="Poole">Poole</a></li></ol>\n</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">\n</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Members of Parliament</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/List_of_Parliamentary_constituencies_in_Dorset" title="List of Parliamentary constituencies in Dorset">List of MPs</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">Police</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Dorset_Police" title="Dorset Police">Dorset Police</a></td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Time_zone" title="Time zone">Time zone</a></th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Mean_Time" title="Greenwich Mean Time">Greenwich Mean Time</a> (<a href="/wiki/UTC%C2%B100:00" title="UTC\xc2\xb100:00">UTC</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row">&#160;\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;Summer (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight saving time">DST</a>)</th><td>\n<a href="/wiki/British_Summer_Time" title="British Summer Time">British Summer Time</a> (<a href="/wiki/UTC%2B01:00" title="UTC+01:00">UTC+1</a>)</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Dorset</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">\xc9\x94\xcb\x90r</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Archaism" title="Archaism">archaically</a>: <b>Dorsetshire</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Counties_of_England" title="Counties of England">county</a> in <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West England</a> on the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> coast. The <a href="/wiki/Ceremonial_counties_of_England" title="Ceremonial counties of England">ceremonial county</a> comprises the <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_county" title="Non-metropolitan county">non-metropolitan county</a>, which is governed by <a href="/wiki/Dorset_County_Council" title="Dorset County Council">Dorset County Council</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority areas</a> of <a href="/wiki/Poole" title="Poole">Poole</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth" title="Bournemouth">Bournemouth</a>. Covering an area of 2,653 square kilometres (1,024&#160;sq&#160;mi), Dorset borders <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a> to the west, <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a> to the north-west, <a href="/wiki/Wiltshire" title="Wiltshire">Wiltshire</a> to the north-east, and <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a> to the east. The <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a> is <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Dorset" title="Dorchester, Dorset">Dorchester</a> which is  in the south. After the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">reorganisation of local government in 1974</a> the county\'s border was extended eastward to incorporate the Hampshire towns of Bournemouth and Christchurch. Around half of the population lives in the <a href="/wiki/South_East_Dorset_conurbation" title="South East Dorset conurbation">South East Dorset conurbation</a>, while the rest of the county is largely rural with a low population density.\n</p><p>The county has a long history of human settlement stretching back to the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> era. The <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">Romans</a> conquered Dorset\'s indigenous <a href="/wiki/Durotriges" title="Durotriges">Celtic tribe</a>, and during the early Middle Ages, the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Saxons</a> settled the area and made Dorset a <a href="/wiki/Shire" title="Shire">shire</a> in the 7th century. The first recorded <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Viking</a> raid on the British Isles occurred in Dorset during the eighth century, and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death_in_England" title="Black Death in England">Black Death</a> entered England at <a href="/wiki/Melcombe_Regis" title="Melcombe Regis">Melcombe Regis</a> in 1348. Dorset has seen much civil unrest: in the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, an uprising of <a href="/wiki/Clubmen" title="Clubmen">vigilantes</a> was crushed by <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Oliver Cromwell</a>\'s forces in a pitched battle near <a href="/wiki/Shaftesbury" title="Shaftesbury">Shaftesbury</a>; the doomed <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_Rebellion" title="Monmouth Rebellion">Monmouth Rebellion</a> began at <a href="/wiki/Lyme_Regis" title="Lyme Regis">Lyme Regis</a>; and a group of farm labourers from <a href="/wiki/Tolpuddle_Martyrs" title="Tolpuddle Martyrs">Tolpuddle</a> were instrumental in the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">trade union movement</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>, Dorset was heavily involved in the preparations for the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Normandy" title="Invasion of Normandy">invasion of Normandy</a>, and the large harbours of <a href="/wiki/Portland_Harbour" title="Portland Harbour">Portland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poole_Harbour" title="Poole Harbour">Poole</a> were two of the main embarkation points. The former was the sailing venue in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a>, and both have clubs or hire venues for <a href="/wiki/Sailing" title="Sailing">sailing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornish_pilot_gig" title="Cornish pilot gig">Cornish pilot gig</a> rowing, <a href="/wiki/Sea_kayak" title="Sea kayak">sea kayaking</a> and <a href="/wiki/Powerboating" title="Powerboating">powerboating</a>.\n</p><p>Dorset has a varied landscape featuring broad elevated <a href="/wiki/Downland" title="Downland">chalk downs</a>, steep limestone ridges and low-lying clay valleys. Over half the county is designated as an <a href="/wiki/Area_of_Outstanding_Natural_Beauty" title="Area of Outstanding Natural Beauty">Area of Outstanding Natural Beauty</a>. Three-quarters of its coastline is part of the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Coast" title="Jurassic Coast">Jurassic Coast</a> Natural <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> due to its geological and palaeontologic significance. It features notable landforms such as <a href="/wiki/Lulworth_Cove" title="Lulworth Cove">Lulworth Cove</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Portland" title="Isle of Portland">Isle of Portland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chesil_Beach" title="Chesil Beach">Chesil Beach</a> and <a href="/wiki/Durdle_Door" title="Durdle Door">Durdle Door</a>. Agriculture was traditionally the major industry of Dorset but is now in decline and tourism has become increasingly important to the economy. There are no motorways in Dorset but a network of <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_road_numbering_scheme#A_roads" title="Great Britain road numbering scheme">A roads</a> cross the county and two railway main lines connect to London. Dorset has ports at Poole, <a href="/wiki/Weymouth,_Dorset" title="Weymouth, Dorset">Weymouth</a> and Portland, and an <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Airport" title="Bournemouth Airport">international airport</a>. The county has a variety of museums, theatres and festivals, and is host to the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dorset_Steam_Fair" title="Great Dorset Steam Fair">Great Dorset Steam Fair</a>, one of the biggest events of its kind in Europe. It is the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hardy" title="Thomas Hardy">Thomas Hardy</a>, who used the county as the principal setting of his novels, and <a href="/wiki/William_Barnes" title="William Barnes">William Barnes</a>, whose poetry celebrates the ancient <a href="/wiki/West_Country_English" title="West Country English">Dorset dialect</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Toponymy"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Toponymy</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Physical geography</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-5"><a href="#Climate"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Climate</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Demography"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Demography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Politics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Politics</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Local_Government"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Local Government</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-9"><a href="#2019_Structural_changes_to_local_government"><span class="tocnumber">6.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">2019 Structural changes to local government</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#National_Representation"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">National Representation</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-11"><a href="#Economy_and_industry"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Economy and industry</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-12"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-13"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Religious_sites"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Religious sites</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">16</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Toponymy">Toponymy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Toponymy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Dorset derives its name from the <a href="/wiki/County_town" title="County town">county town</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Dorset" title="Dorchester, Dorset">Dorchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-place_names_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-place_names-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Romans</a> established the settlement in the 1st century and named it <a href="/wiki/Durnovaria" title="Durnovaria">Durnovaria</a> which was a Latinised version of a <a href="/wiki/Common_Brittonic" title="Common Brittonic">Common Brittonic</a> word possibly meaning "place with fist-sized pebbles".<sup id="cite_ref-place_names_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-place_names-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxons" title="Anglo-Saxons">Saxons</a> named the town Dornwaraceaster (the suffix "ceaster" being the <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> name for a Roman town) and Dorns\xc3\xa6te came into use as the name for the inhabitants of the area from "Dorn"\xe2\x80\x94a reduced form of Dornwaraceaster\xe2\x80\x94and the Old English word "s\xc3\xa6te" meaning people.<sup id="cite_ref-place_names_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-place_names-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It is first mentioned in the <i><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_Chronicle" title="Anglo-Saxon Chronicle">Anglo-Saxon Chronicle</a></i> in AD&#160;845 and in the 10th century the county\'s archaic name, "Dorseteschyre" (Dorsetshire), was first recorded.<sup id="cite_ref-DCM_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCM-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Dorset" title="History of Dorset">History of Dorset</a></div>\n<p>The first human visitors to Dorset were <a href="/wiki/Mesolithic" title="Mesolithic">Mesolithic</a> hunters, from around 8000&#160;<a href="/wiki/Before_Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Before Christ">BC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Put15_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Put15-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_p13_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_p13-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> The first permanent <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic</a> settlers appeared around 3000&#160;BC and were responsible for the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Dorset_Cursus" title="Dorset Cursus">Dorset Cursus</a>, a 10.5-kilometre (6.5&#160;mi) monument for ritual or ceremonial purposes.<sup id="cite_ref-Put19_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Put19-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_p.14_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_p.14-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> From 2800&#160;BC onwards <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> farmers cleared Dorset\'s woodlands for agricultural use and Dorset\'s high chalk hills provided a location for numerous <a href="/wiki/Round_barrows" class="mw-redirect" title="Round barrows">round barrows</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_Culture_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_Culture-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Britons_(Celtic_people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (Celtic people)">British</a> tribe known as the <a href="/wiki/Durotriges" title="Durotriges">Durotriges</a> established a series of <a href="/wiki/Hill_fort" class="mw-redirect" title="Hill fort">hill forts</a> across the county\xe2\x80\x94most notably <a href="/wiki/Maiden_Castle,_Dorset" title="Maiden Castle, Dorset">Maiden Castle</a> which is one of the largest in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_p.16_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_p.16-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Romans arrived in Dorset during their <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">conquest of Britain</a> in AD&#160;43. Maiden Castle was captured by a <a href="/wiki/Legio_II_Augusta" title="Legio II Augusta">Roman legion</a> under the command of <a href="/wiki/Vespasian" title="Vespasian">Vespasian</a>, and the Roman settlement of Durnovaria was established nearby.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vespasian_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vespasian-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bokerley_Dyke" title="Bokerley Dyke">Bokerley Dyke</a>, a large defensive ditch built by the county\'s post-Roman inhabitants near the border with modern-day <a href="/wiki/Hampshire" title="Hampshire">Hampshire</a>, delayed the advance of the Saxons into Dorset for almost 150 years.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> However, by the end of the 7th century Dorset had fallen under Saxon control and been incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Wessex" class="mw-redirect" title="Kingdom of Wessex">Kingdom of Wessex</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Draper142_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draper142-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The Saxons established a <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Salisbury" title="Diocese of Salisbury">diocese</a> at <a href="/wiki/Sherborne" title="Sherborne">Sherborne</a> and Dorset was made a <a href="/wiki/Shire" title="Shire">shire</a>\xe2\x80\x94an administrative district of Wessex and predecessor to the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_counties_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient counties of England">English county</a> system\xe2\x80\x94with borders that have changed little since.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 789 the first recorded <a href="/wiki/Viking" class="mw-redirect" title="Viking">Viking</a> attack on the British Isles took place in Dorset on the Portland coast, and they continued to raid into the county for the next two centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest_of_England" title="Norman conquest of England">Norman Conquest</a> in 1066, <a href="/wiki/Feudalism_in_England" title="Feudalism in England">feudal</a> rule was established in Dorset and the bulk of the land was divided between the Crown and ecclesiastical institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The Normans consolidated their control over the area by constructing castles at <a href="/wiki/Corfe_Castle" title="Corfe Castle">Corfe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wareham_Castle" class="mw-redirect" title="Wareham Castle">Wareham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dorchester_Castle" title="Dorchester Castle">Dorchester</a> in the early part of the 12th century.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Over the next 200 years Dorset\'s population grew substantially and additional land was enclosed for farming to provide the extra food required.<sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_p52_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_p52-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The wool trade, the quarrying of <a href="/wiki/Purbeck_Marble" title="Purbeck Marble">Purbeck Marble</a> and the busy ports of <a href="/wiki/Weymouth,_Dorset" title="Weymouth, Dorset">Weymouth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melcombe_Regis" title="Melcombe Regis">Melcombe Regis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyme_Regis" title="Lyme Regis">Lyme Regis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bridport" title="Bridport">Bridport</a> brought prosperity to the county.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> However, Dorset was devastated by the bubonic plague in 1348 which arrived in Melcombe Regis on a ship from <a href="/wiki/Gascony" title="Gascony">Gascony</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The disease, more commonly known as the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>, created an epidemic that spread rapidly and wiped out a third of the population of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Corfe_Castle3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="the ruins of Corfe Castle" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Corfe_Castle3.jpg/220px-Corfe_Castle3.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Corfe_Castle3.jpg/330px-Corfe_Castle3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Corfe_Castle3.jpg/440px-Corfe_Castle3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="1877" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Corfe_Castle3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Corfe_Castle" title="Corfe Castle">Corfe Castle</a>, captured and destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Cromwell" title="Oliver Cromwell">Cromwell\'s</a> army in 1646</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_monasteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Dissolution of the monasteries">dissolution of the monasteries</a> (1536\xe2\x80\x931541) met little resistance in Dorset and many of the county\'s abbeys, including <a href="/wiki/Shaftesbury_Abbey" title="Shaftesbury Abbey">Shaftesbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cerne_Abbey" title="Cerne Abbey">Cerne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milton_Abbey_School#Abbey_church" title="Milton Abbey School">Milton</a>, were sold to private owners.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> In 1642, at the commencement of the <a href="/wiki/English_Civil_War" title="English Civil War">English Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cavalier" title="Cavalier">Royalists</a> took control of the entire county apart from Poole and Lyme Regis. However, within three years their gains had been almost entirely reversed by the <a href="/wiki/Roundhead" title="Roundhead">Parliamentarians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> An uprising of <a href="/wiki/Clubmen" title="Clubmen">Clubmen</a>\xe2\x80\x94vigilantes weary of the depredations of the war\xe2\x80\x94took place in Dorset in 1645. Some 2,000 of these rebels offered battle to <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fairfax,_3rd_Lord_Fairfax_of_Cameron" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Fairfax, 3rd Lord Fairfax of Cameron">Lord Fairfax\'s</a> Parliamentary army at <a href="/wiki/Hambledon_Hill" title="Hambledon Hill">Hambledon Hill</a> but they were easily routed.<sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_pp70\xe2\x80\x9371_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_pp70\xe2\x80\x9371-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sherborne_Castle" title="Sherborne Castle">Sherborne Castle</a> was taken by Fairfax that same year and in 1646 Corfe Castle, the last remaining Royalist stronghold in Dorset, was captured after an act of betrayal: both were subsequently <a href="/wiki/Slighting" title="Slighting">slighted</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_pp70\xe2\x80\x9371_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_pp70\xe2\x80\x9371-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/James_Scott,_1st_Duke_of_Monmouth" title="James Scott, 1st Duke of Monmouth">Duke of Monmouth\'s</a> unsuccessful <a href="/wiki/Monmouth_Rebellion" title="Monmouth Rebellion">attempt to overthrow James II</a> began when he landed at Lyme Regis in 1685.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> A series of trials known as the <a href="/wiki/Bloody_Assizes" title="Bloody Assizes">Bloody Assizes</a> took place to punish the rebels. Over a five-day period in Dorchester, <a href="/wiki/Judge_Jeffreys" class="mw-redirect" title="Judge Jeffreys">Judge Jeffreys</a> presided over 312 cases: 74 of the accused were executed, 175 were <a href="/wiki/Penal_transportation" title="Penal transportation">transported</a>, and nine were publicly whipped.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In 1686, at <a href="/wiki/Charborough_House" title="Charborough House">Charborough Park</a>, a meeting took place to plot the downfall of <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James II of England</a>. This meeting was effectively the start of the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 18th century, much <a href="/wiki/Smuggling" title="Smuggling">smuggling</a> took place along the Dorset coast; its coves, caves and sandy beaches provided opportunities for gangs such as the <a href="/wiki/Hawkhurst_Gang" title="Hawkhurst Gang">Hawkhursts</a> to stealthily bring smuggled goods ashore.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Poole became Dorset\'s busiest port and established prosperous trade links with the fisheries of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> which supported cloth, rope and net manufacturing industries in the surrounding towns and villages.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_revolution" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial revolution">industrial revolution</a> largely bypassed Dorset which lacked coal resources and as a consequence the county remained predominantly agricultural.<sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_p105_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_p105-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Draper143_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draper143-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Farming has always been central to the economy of Dorset and the county became the birthplace of the modern <a href="/wiki/Trade_union_movement" class="mw-redirect" title="Trade union movement">trade union movement</a> when, in 1834, six farm labourers formed a union to protest against falling wages. The labourers, who are now known as the <a href="/wiki/Tolpuddle_Martyrs" title="Tolpuddle Martyrs">Tolpuddle Martyrs</a>, were subsequently arrested for administering "unlawful oaths" and sentenced to transportation but they were pardoned following massive protests by the working classes.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dorsetshire_Regiment" class="mw-redirect" title="Dorsetshire Regiment">Dorsetshire Regiment</a> were the first British unit to face a <a href="/wiki/Chemical_weapons_in_World_War_I" title="Chemical weapons in World War I">gas attack</a> during the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a> (1914\xe2\x80\x931918) and they sustained particularly heavy losses at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Somme" title="Battle of the Somme">Battle of the Somme</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc_somme_memorial_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_somme_memorial-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> In total some 4,500 Dorset servicemen died in the war and of the county\'s towns and villages, only one, <a href="/wiki/Langton_Herring" title="Langton Herring">Langton Herring</a>, known as a <a href="/wiki/Thankful_Villages" title="Thankful Villages">Thankful Village</a>, had no residents killed.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc_somme_memorial_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc_somme_memorial-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> (1939\xe2\x80\x931945) Dorset was heavily involved in the preparations for the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Normandy" title="Invasion of Normandy">invasion of Normandy</a>: beach landing exercises were carried out at <a href="/wiki/Studland" title="Studland">Studland</a> and Weymouth and the village of <a href="/wiki/Tyneham" title="Tyneham">Tyneham</a> was requisitioned for army training.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Tens-of-thousands of troops departed Weymouth, Portland and Poole harbours during <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">D-Day</a> and gliders from <a href="/wiki/RAF_Tarrant_Rushton" title="RAF Tarrant Rushton">RAF Tarrant Rushton</a> dropped troops near <a href="/wiki/Caen" title="Caen">Caen</a> to begin <a href="/wiki/Operation_Tonga" title="Operation Tonga">Operation Tonga</a>. Dorset experienced an increase in holiday-makers after the war.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> First popularised as a tourist destination by <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">George III\'s</a> frequent visits to Weymouth, the county\'s coastline, seaside resorts and its sparsely populated rural areas attract millions of visitors each year.<sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_p105_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_p105-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> With farming declining across the country, tourism has edged ahead as the primary revenue-earning sector.<sup id="cite_ref-Draper143_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draper143-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Settlements">Settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Settlements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_in_Dorset" title="List of places in Dorset">List of places in Dorset</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_settlements_in_Dorset_by_population" title="List of settlements in Dorset by population">List of settlements in Dorset by population</a></div>\n<div class="noviewer thumb style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Gillingham" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/8px-Red_pog.svg.png" title="Gillingham" width="8" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;right:5px;text-align:right"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:right;background-color:white"><a href="/wiki/Gillingham,_Dorset" title="Gillingham, Dorset">Gillingham</a></div></div></div><div style="position:absolute;top:15.567%;left:59.104%"><div style="position:absolute;left:-4px;top:-4px;line-height:0"><img alt="Shaftesbury" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/12px-Red_pog.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Red_pog.svg/16px-Red_pog.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="64" data-file-height="64" /></div><div style="font-size:90%;line-height:110%;position:absolute;width:6em;top:-0.75em;left:5px;text-align:left"><div style="display:inline;padding:1px;float:left;background-color:white"><a href="/wiki/Shaftesbury" title="Shaftesbury">Shaftesbury</a></div></div></div></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dorset_UK_location_map.svg" title="File:Dorset UK location map.svg"> </a></div>Some of the larger settlements of Dorset</div></div></div>\n<p>Dorset is largely rural with many small villages, few large towns and no cities.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Minerals_Core_Strategy_p20_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minerals_Core_Strategy_p20-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The only major urban area is the <a href="/wiki/South_East_Dorset_conurbation" title="South East Dorset conurbation">South East Dorset conurbation</a>, which is situated at the south-eastern end of the county and is atypical of the county as a whole. It consists of the <a href="/wiki/Seaside_resort" title="Seaside resort">seaside resort</a> of Bournemouth, the historic port and <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">borough</a> of Poole, the towns of Christchurch and <a href="/wiki/Ferndown" title="Ferndown">Ferndown</a> plus many surrounding villages.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Bournemouth, the most populous town in the conurbation, was established in the <a href="/wiki/Georgian_era" title="Georgian era">Georgian era</a> when <a href="/wiki/Sea_bathing" title="Sea bathing">sea bathing</a> became popular.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> Poole, the second largest settlement (once the largest town in the county), adjoins Bournemouth to the west and contains the suburb of <a href="/wiki/Sandbanks" title="Sandbanks">Sandbanks</a> which has some of the highest land values by area in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-sandbanks_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sandbanks-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The other two major settlements in the county are Dorchester, which has been the county town since at least 1305,<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and Weymouth, a major seaside resort since the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_Pop_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_Pop-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DFY_Weymouth_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_Weymouth-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Blandford_Forum" title="Blandford Forum">Blandford Forum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sherborne" title="Sherborne">Sherborne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gillingham,_Dorset" title="Gillingham, Dorset">Gillingham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shaftesbury" title="Shaftesbury">Shaftesbury</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sturminster_Newton" title="Sturminster Newton">Sturminster Newton</a> are historic <a href="/wiki/Market_town" title="Market town">market towns</a> which serve the farms and villages of the <a href="/wiki/Blackmore_Vale" title="Blackmore Vale">Blackmore Vale</a> in north Dorset.<sup id="cite_ref-MKT_Towns_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MKT_Towns-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Beaminster" title="Beaminster">Beaminster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bridport" title="Bridport">Bridport</a> are situated in the west of the county; <a href="/wiki/Verwood" title="Verwood">Verwood</a> and the historic Saxon market towns of <a href="/wiki/Wareham,_Dorset" title="Wareham, Dorset">Wareham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wimborne_Minster" title="Wimborne Minster">Wimborne Minster</a> are located to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-MKT_Towns_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MKT_Towns-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Lyme Regis and <a href="/wiki/Swanage" title="Swanage">Swanage</a> are small coastal towns popular with tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-Coastal_Towns_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coastal_Towns-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Under construction on the western edge of Dorchester is the experimental <a href="/wiki/New_town" class="mw-redirect" title="New town">new town</a> of <a href="/wiki/Poundbury" title="Poundbury">Poundbury</a> commissioned and co-designed by <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Charles, Prince of Wales">Prince Charles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The suburb, which is expected to be fully completed by 2025, was designed to integrate residential and retail buildings and counter the growth of <a href="/wiki/Dormitory_town" class="mw-redirect" title="Dormitory town">dormitory towns</a> and car-oriented development.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Dorset" title="Geography of Dorset">Geography of Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Dorset" title="Geology of Dorset">Geology of Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_hills_of_Dorset" title="List of hills of Dorset">List of hills of Dorset</a>, and <a href="/wiki/South_West_Hampshire/South_East_Dorset_Green_Belt" title="South West Hampshire/South East Dorset Green Belt">South West Hampshire/South East Dorset Green Belt</a></div>\n<p>Dorset covers an area of 2,653 square kilometres (1,024&#160;sq&#160;mi) and contains considerable variety in its underlying geology, which is partly responsible for the diversity of landscape.<sup id="cite_ref-DDB_2010_p8_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DDB_2010_p8-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Draper_136_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draper_136-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> A large percentage (66%) of the county comprises either <a href="/wiki/Chalk" title="Chalk">chalk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clay</a> or mixed <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gravel" title="Gravel">gravels</a>. The remainder is less straightforward and includes <a href="/wiki/Portland_stone" title="Portland stone">Portland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Purbeck_Group" title="Purbeck Group">Purbeck stone</a>, other <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calcareous_clay" class="mw-redirect" title="Calcareous clay">calcareous clays</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">shales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Draper_136/137_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draper_136/137-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Portland and Purbeck stone are of national importance as a building material and for restoring some of Britain\'s most famous landmarks.<sup id="cite_ref-Minerals_Core_Strategy_p22_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minerals_Core_Strategy_p22-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Almost every type of rock known from the <a href="/wiki/Early_Jurassic" title="Early Jurassic">Early Jurassic</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a> epochs can be found in the county.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Geology_of_Britain_Viewer_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geology_of_Britain_Viewer-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dorset_Geology.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Dorset_Geology.png/300px-Dorset_Geology.png" width="300" height="208" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Dorset_Geology.png/450px-Dorset_Geology.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Dorset_Geology.png/600px-Dorset_Geology.png 2x" data-file-width="1156" data-file-height="801" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dorset_Geology.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Geological map of Dorset</div></div></div>\n<p>Dorset has a number of limestone ridges which are mostly covered in either arable fields or <a href="/wiki/Calcareous_grassland" title="Calcareous grassland">calcareous grassland</a> supporting sheep.<sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_p.91_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_p.91-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> These limestone areas include a wide band of <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> chalk which crosses the county as a range of hills from north-east to south-west, incorporating <a href="/wiki/Cranborne_Chase" title="Cranborne Chase">Cranborne Chase</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dorset_Downs" title="Dorset Downs">Dorset Downs</a>, and a narrow band running from south-west to south-east, incorporating the <a href="/wiki/Purbeck_Hills" title="Purbeck Hills">Purbeck Hills</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chaffey_43_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chaffey_43-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chaffey_11_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chaffey_11-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Between the chalk hills are large, wide <a href="/wiki/River_valley" class="mw-redirect" title="River valley">vales</a> and wide <a href="/wiki/Flood_plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Flood plain">flood plains</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Geology_of_Britain_Viewer_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geology_of_Britain_Viewer-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> These vales are dotted with small villages, farms and <a href="/wiki/Coppice" class="mw-redirect" title="Coppice">coppices</a>, and include the <a href="/wiki/Blackmore_Vale" title="Blackmore Vale">Blackmore Vale</a> (<a href="/wiki/River_Stour,_Dorset" title="River Stour, Dorset">Stour valley</a>) and <a href="/wiki/River_Frome,_Dorset" title="River Frome, Dorset">Frome valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Chaffey_11_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chaffey_11-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The Blackmore Vale is composed of older Jurassic deposits, largely clays interspersed with limestones,<sup id="cite_ref-Geology_of_Britain_Viewer_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geology_of_Britain_Viewer-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and has traditionally been a centre for dairy agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> South-east Dorset, including the lower Frome valley and around Poole and Bournemouth, comprises younger Eocene deposits,<sup id="cite_ref-Geology_of_Britain_Viewer_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Geology_of_Britain_Viewer-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> mainly sands and clays of poor agricultural quality.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The soils created from these deposits support a <a href="/wiki/Heathland" class="mw-redirect" title="Heathland">heathland</a> habitat which sustains all six native <a href="/wiki/List_of_reptiles_of_Great_Britain" title="List of reptiles of Great Britain">British reptile</a> species.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> Most of the Dorset heathland has <a href="/wiki/SSSI" class="mw-redirect" title="SSSI">Site of Special Scientific Interest</a> (SSSI) status with three areas designated as internationally important <a href="/wiki/Ramsar_Convention" title="Ramsar Convention">Ramsar sites</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In the far west of the county and along the coast there are frequent changes in rock strata, which appear in a less obviously sequential way compared to the landscapes of the chalk and the heath.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> In the west this results in a hilly landscape of diverse character that resembles that of neighbouring county <a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Marshwood_Vale" title="Marshwood Vale">Marshwood Vale</a>, a valley of <a href="/wiki/Lower_Lias" class="mw-redirect" title="Lower Lias">Lower Lias</a> clay at the western tip of the county,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> lies to the south of the two highest points in Dorset: <a href="/wiki/Lewesdon_Hill" title="Lewesdon Hill">Lewesdon Hill</a> at 279 metres (915&#160;ft) and <a href="/wiki/Pilsdon_Pen" title="Pilsdon Pen">Pilsdon Pen</a> at 277 metres (909&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A former river valley flooded by rising sea levels 6,000 years ago, <a href="/wiki/Poole_Harbour" title="Poole Harbour">Poole Harbour</a> is one of the largest natural harbours in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\nThe harbour is very shallow in places and contains a number of islands, notably <a href="/wiki/Brownsea_Island" title="Brownsea Island">Brownsea Island</a>, the birthplace of the <a href="/wiki/Scouting" title="Scouting">Scouting</a> movement and one of the few remaining sanctuaries for indigenous <a href="/wiki/Red_squirrel" title="Red squirrel">red squirrels</a> in England.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> The harbour, and the chalk and limestone hills of the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Purbeck" title="Isle of Purbeck">Isle of Purbeck</a> to the south, lie atop Western Europe\'s largest onshore <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil field">oil field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WFAP_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WFAP-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The field, operated by <a href="/wiki/Perenco" title="Perenco">Perenco</a> from <a href="/wiki/Wytch_Farm" title="Wytch Farm">Wytch Farm</a>, has the world\'s oldest continuously pumping well at <a href="/wiki/Kimmeridge_Oil_Field" title="Kimmeridge Oil Field">Kimmeridge</a> which has been producing oil since the early 1960s.<sup id="cite_ref-WFAP_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WFAP-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cullingford_p.122_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cullingford_p.122-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorset\'s diverse geography ensures it has an assortment of rivers, although a moderate annual rainfall coupled with rolling hills, means most are typically <a href="/wiki/Lowland" class="mw-redirect" title="Lowland">lowland</a> in nature.<sup id="cite_ref-Wright_7_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wright_7-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Much of the county drains into three rivers, the <a href="/wiki/River_Frome,_Dorset" title="River Frome, Dorset">Frome</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Piddle" title="River Piddle">Piddle</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Stour,_Dorset" title="River Stour, Dorset">Stour</a> which all flow to the sea in a south-easterly direction.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The Frome and Piddle are <a href="/wiki/Chalk_stream" title="Chalk stream">chalk streams</a> but the Stour, which rises in Wiltshire to the north, has its origins in clay soil.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Hampshire_Avon" class="mw-redirect" title="Hampshire Avon">River Avon</a>, which flows mainly through Wiltshire and Hampshire, enters Dorset towards the end of its journey at <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Harbour" title="Christchurch Harbour">Christchurch Harbour</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The rivers <a href="/wiki/River_Axe_(Lyme_Bay)" title="River Axe (Lyme Bay)">Axe</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Yeo_(South_Somerset)" title="River Yeo (South Somerset)">Yeo</a>, which principally drain the counties of Devon and <a href="/wiki/Somerset" title="Somerset">Somerset</a> respectively, have their sources in the north-west of the county. In the south-west, a number of small rivers run into the sea along the Dorset coastline; most notable of these are the <a href="/wiki/River_Char" title="River Char">Char</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Brit" title="River Brit">Brit</a>, <a href="/wiki/River_Bride,_Dorset" title="River Bride, Dorset">Bride</a> and <a href="/wiki/River_Wey,_Dorset" title="River Wey, Dorset">Wey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wright_17_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wright_17-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Durdle_Door_Overview.jpg" class="image"><img alt="photograph of Durdle Door arch near Lulworth" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Durdle_Door_Overview.jpg/260px-Durdle_Door_Overview.jpg" width="260" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Durdle_Door_Overview.jpg/390px-Durdle_Door_Overview.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Durdle_Door_Overview.jpg/520px-Durdle_Door_Overview.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3996" data-file-height="2616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Durdle_Door_Overview.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Durdle_Door" title="Durdle Door">Durdle Door</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Natural_arch" title="Natural arch">natural arch</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lulworth_Cove" title="Lulworth Cove">Lulworth Cove</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Most of Dorset\'s coastline is part of the <a href="/wiki/Jurassic_Coast" title="Jurassic Coast">Jurassic Coast</a>, a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a>, which stretches for 155 kilometres (96&#160;mi)<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> between Studland and <a href="/wiki/Exmouth" title="Exmouth">Exmouth</a> in Devon. This coast documents the entire <a href="/wiki/Mesozoic" title="Mesozoic">Mesozoic</a> era, from <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a> to <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> and is noted for its geological <a href="/wiki/Landform" title="Landform">landforms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcjurassic_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcjurassic-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The Dorset section has yielded important fossils, including <a href="/wiki/Petrified_wood" title="Petrified wood">Jurassic trees</a> and the first complete <a href="/wiki/Ichthyosaur" title="Ichthyosaur">Ichthyosaur</a>, discovered near <a href="/wiki/Lyme_Regis" title="Lyme Regis">Lyme Regis</a> in 1811 by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Anning" title="Mary Anning">Mary Anning</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbcjurassic_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbcjurassic-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The county features some notable coastal landforms, including examples of a <a href="/wiki/Cove" title="Cove">cove</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lulworth_Cove" title="Lulworth Cove">Lulworth Cove</a>), a <a href="/wiki/Natural_arch" title="Natural arch">natural arch</a> (<a href="/wiki/Durdle_Door" title="Durdle Door">Durdle Door</a>) and chalk <a href="/wiki/Stack_(geology)" title="Stack (geology)">stacks</a> (<a href="/wiki/Old_Harry_Rocks" title="Old Harry Rocks">Old Harry Rocks</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Jutting out into the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> at roughly the midpoint of the Dorset coastline is the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Portland" title="Isle of Portland">Isle of Portland</a>, a limestone island that is connected to the mainland by <a href="/wiki/Chesil_Beach" title="Chesil Beach">Chesil Beach</a>, a 27-kilometre (17&#160;mi) long <a href="/wiki/Shingle_beach" title="Shingle beach">shingle</a> <a href="/wiki/Shoal" title="Shoal">barrier beach</a> protecting <a href="/wiki/Chesil_Beach#The_Fleet_Lagoon" title="Chesil Beach">Britain\'s largest tidal lagoon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The county has one of the highest proportions of <a href="/wiki/Conservation_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Conservation area">conservation areas</a> in England\xe2\x80\x94and two <a href="/wiki/AONB" class="mw-redirect" title="AONB">Areas of Outstanding Natural Beauty</a> (AONB) covering 53% of the administrative county.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> It has two <a href="/wiki/Heritage_Coast" class="mw-redirect" title="Heritage Coast">Heritage Coasts</a> totalling 92 kilometres (57&#160;mi) and Sites of Special Scientific Interest covering 199&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (77&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-coastline_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coastline-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sssi_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sssi-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/South_West_Coast_Path" title="South West Coast Path">South West Coast Path</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Trail" class="mw-redirect" title="National Trail">National Trail</a>, begins at South Haven Point at the entrance to Poole Harbour.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> There are also substantial areas of <a href="/wiki/Green_belt_(United_Kingdom)" title="Green belt (United Kingdom)">green belt</a> surrounding the <a href="/wiki/South_East_Dorset_conurbation" title="South East Dorset conurbation">South East Dorset conurbation</a>, filling in the area between this and the <a href="/wiki/Cranborne_Chase" title="Cranborne Chase">Cranborne Chase and the West Wiltshire Downs</a> AONB.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Dorset\'s climate of warm summers and mild winters is partly due to its position on Britain\'s south coast. The third most southerly county in the UK, Dorset is less affected by the more intense Atlantic winds than <a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a> and Devon. Dorset, along with the entire south-west, has higher winter temperatures, average 4.5 to 8.7&#160;\xc2\xb0C (40.1 to 47.7&#160;\xc2\xb0F), than the rest of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-winter_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-winter-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> However, Dorset maintains higher summer temperatures than Devon and Cornwall, with average highs of 19.1 to 22.2&#160;\xc2\xb0C (66.4 to 72.0&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-summer_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-summer-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Excluding hills such as the Dorset Downs, the average annual temperature of the county is 9.8 to 12&#160;\xc2\xb0C (49.6 to 53.6&#160;\xc2\xb0F).<sup id="cite_ref-annual_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-annual-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The south coast counties of Dorset, Hampshire, <a href="/wiki/West_Sussex" title="West Sussex">West Sussex</a>, East Sussex and <a href="/wiki/Kent" title="Kent">Kent</a> enjoy more sunshine than anywhere else in the United Kingdom, receiving 1,541\xe2\x80\x931,885 hours a year.<sup id="cite_ref-sunshine_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sunshine-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Average annual rainfall varies across the county\xe2\x80\x94southern and eastern coastal areas receive 700\xe2\x80\x93800 millimetres (28\xe2\x80\x9331 inches) per year; the Dorset Downs receive between 1,000 and 1,250 millimetres (39 and 49 inches) per year; less than Devon and Cornwall to the west but more than counties to the east.<sup id="cite_ref-rainfall_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rainfall-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable collapsible" style="width:90%; text-align:center; font-size:90%; line-height: 1.2em; margin:auto;">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="14">Climate data for Weymouth\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Month\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jan\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Feb\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Mar\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Apr\n</th>\n<th scope="col">May\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jun\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Jul\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Aug\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Sep\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Oct\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Nov\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Dec\n</th>\n<th scope="col" style="border-left-width:medium">Year\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="text-align: center;">\n<th scope="row" style="height: 16px;">Average high \xc2\xb0C (\xc2\xb0F)\n</th>\n<td style="background: #FFE2C6; color:#000000;">8.6<br /> (47.5)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFE4C9; color:#000000;">8.4<br /> (47.1)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFD7B0; color:#000000;">10.2<br /> (50.4)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFC993; color:#000000;">12.3<br /> (54.1)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFB46A; color:#000000;">15.3<br /> (59.5)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FFA449; color:#000000;">17.7<br /> (63.9)\n</td>\n<td style="background: #FF962D; class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Demography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_settlements_in_Dorset_by_population" title="List of settlements in Dorset by population">List of settlements in Dorset by population</a></div>\n<table class="wikitable floatright" style="text-align:center; font-size:95%;" width="50%">\n<caption>Dorset ethnicity and religion\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col"><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">UK Census 2011</a>\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Dorset<sup class="reference plainlinks nourlexpansion" id="ref_a"><a href="#endnote_a">note</a></sup><br /><sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Dorset_ethnic_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Bournemouth_religion-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Poole<br /><sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Poole_ethnic_115-0" class="reference"><a id="cite_ref-ONS_Dorset_ethnic_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Dorset_ethnic-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Dorset_religion_112-1" class="reference"><a religion\n</th>\n<td>25.2%</td>\n<td>30.5%</td>\n<td>29.7%</td>\n<td>29.3%</td>\n<td>24.7%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Not stated\n</th>\n<td>8.0%</td>\n<td>7.8%</td>\n<td>7.6%</td>\n<td>7.9%</td>\n<td>7.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="center" colspan="30" style="font-size: 8pt"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_a"><b><a href="#ref_a">^</a></b></span> Excluding Bournemouth and Poole\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Census_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="United Kingdom Census 2011">2011 Census</a> records Dorset\'s population as 744,041. This consisted of 412,905 for the <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_county" title="Non-metropolitan county">non-metropolitan county</a> (not including Bournemouth and Poole), 183,491 for the <a href="/wiki/Unitary_authority" title="Unitary authority">unitary authority</a> of Bournemouth and 147,645 for the unitary authority of Poole.<sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Dorset_ethnic_111-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Dorset_ethnic-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Bournemouth_ethnic_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Bournemouth_ethnic-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Poole_ethnic_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Poole_ethnic-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 it was estimated that the population had risen by around 1.4% to 754,460: 416,720 in the non-metropolitan county and 188,730 and 149,010 in Bournemouth and Poole respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-dorsetpopulation_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dorsetpopulation-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> More than half of the county\'s residents live in the Bournemouth, Poole and Christchurch conurbation.<sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Dorset_ethnic_111-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Dorset_ethnic-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorset\'s population has a high proportion of older people and a lower than average proportion of young people: According to 2013 mid-year estimates,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;Note 1&#93;</a></sup> 23.6% are over 65 years of age, higher than the <a href="/wiki/England_and_Wales" title="England and Wales">England and Wales</a> average of 17.4%, and 18.6% are less than 17 years old, lower than the England and Wales average of 21.3%.<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_Pop_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_Pop-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The working age population (females and males between 16 and 64) is lower than England and Wales average, 60% compared to 64%.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Data collected between 2010 and 2012 shows that average life expectancy at birth in the county is 85.3 years for females and 81.2 years for males. This compares favourably with the averages for England and Wales of 82.9 and 79.1 years respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> Around 95.2% of Dorset\'s population are of white ethnicity, 60.9% of the population are <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Christianity in the United Kingdom">Christian</a> and 28.5% say they are not religious.<sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Dorset_ethnic_111-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Dorset_ethnic-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Dorset_religion_112-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Dorset_religion-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>More than 33% of the county\xe2\x80\x99s population possess a level 4 qualification or above, such as a Higher National Diploma, Degree or a Higher Degree; while nearly 6.3% have no qualifications at all.<sup id="cite_ref-Labprof_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Labprof-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Almost 43.7% are employed in a professional or technical capacity (Standard Occupational Classification 2010, groups 1\xe2\x80\x933), just over 10.3% are administrators or secretaries (group 4), around 12.8% have a skilled trade (group 5), over 18% are employed at a low-level in the care, leisure, sales or customer relations sector (groups 6 and 7) and 14.8% are operatives or in elementary occupations (groups 8 and 9).<sup id="cite_ref-Labprof_121-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Labprof-121">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table
