style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+0.55%</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td colspan="4" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">Pre-1974 statistics were gathered from local government areas that now comprise Dorset<br /><i>Source: <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Historical_GIS" title="Great Britain Historical GIS">Great Britain Historical GIS</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Local_Government">Local Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Local Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Local_government_in_England" title="Local government in England">Local government</a> in Dorset consists of a <a href="/wiki/County_council" title="County council">county council</a> (<a href="/wiki/Dorset_County_Council" title="Dorset County Council">Dorset County Council</a>) and two unitary authorities (<a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Borough_Council" title="Bournemouth Borough Council">Bournemouth Borough Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poole_Borough_Council" title="Poole Borough Council">Poole Borough Council</a>). Dorset County Council was created by the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1888" title="Local Government Act 1888">Local Government Act 1888</a> to govern the newly created <a href="/wiki/Administrative_counties_of_England" title="Administrative counties of England">administrative county</a> of Dorset which was based largely on the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_counties_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient counties of England">historic county</a> borders. Dorset became a two-tier non-metropolitan county after a <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Act_1972" title="Local Government Act 1972">reorganisation of local government in 1974</a> and its border was extended eastwards to incorporate the former Hampshire towns of Bournemouth and Christchurch.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;Note 2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Census200_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census200-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> Following a review by the <a href="/wiki/Local_Government_Commission_for_England_(1992)" title="Local Government Commission for England (1992)">Local Government Commission for England</a>, Bournemouth and Poole each became administratively independent single-tier unitary authorities in 1997, although they remain part of the county geographically and for ceremonial purposes. The county council is based in Dorchester and comprises six-second-tier <a href="/wiki/Non-metropolitan_district" title="Non-metropolitan district">districts</a>: <a href="/wiki/West_Dorset" title="West Dorset">West Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/East_Dorset" title="East Dorset">East Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dorset" title="North Dorset">North Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purbeck_(district)" class="mw-redirect" title="Purbeck (district)">Purbeck</a>, Christchurch, and <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_and_Portland" title="Weymouth and Portland">Weymouth and Portland</a>. The council is controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Conservative_Party_(UK)" title="Conservative Party (UK)">Conservative Party</a>: at the <a href="/wiki/Dorset_County_Council_election,_2017" title="Dorset County Council election, 2017">2017 local elections</a> 32 Conservative, 11  <a href="/wiki/Liberal_Democrats_(UK)" title="Liberal Democrats (UK)">Liberal Democrat</a>, 1 <a href="/wiki/Labour_Party_(UK)" title="Labour Party (UK)">Labour</a> and 2  Green Party county councillors were elected.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The Conservatives also have control of Bournemouth and Poole. At the Bournemouth Council election in 2015:  51 Conservative, one Green Party, one <a href="/wiki/UK_Independence_Party" title="UK Independence Party">UK Independence Party</a> and one independent councillors were elected.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>  As of 2015 Poole council comprises 32 Conservative councillors, six Liberal Democrat, three Poole People (a political party of Poole residents) and one <a href="/wiki/UKIP" class="mw-redirect" title="UKIP">UKIP</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>\n<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2019_Structural_changes_to_local_government">2019 Structural changes to local government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2019 Structural changes to local government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Statutory Instruments for local government reorganisation in the ceremonial county of Dorset were made in May 2018. Under the plans, dubbed "Future Dorset", all existing councils within the county will be abolished and replaced by two new unitary authorities. One will be formed from the existing unitary authorities of <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Borough_Council" title="Bournemouth Borough Council">Bournemouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poole_Borough_Council" title="Poole Borough Council">Poole</a> which will merge with the non-metropolitan district of <a href="/wiki/Christchurch,_Dorset" title="Christchurch, Dorset">Christchurch</a> to create a unitary authority to be known as <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth,_Christchurch_and_Poole_Council" title="Bournemouth, Christchurch and Poole Council">Bournemouth, Christchurch and Poole Council</a>. The other will be created from the merger of the existing non-metropolitan districts of <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_and_Portland" title="Weymouth and Portland">Weymouth and Portland</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Dorset" title="West Dorset">West Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/North_Dorset" title="North Dorset">North Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/Purbeck_District" title="Purbeck District">Purbeck</a> and <a href="/wiki/East_Dorset" title="East Dorset">East Dorset</a> and will be known as <a href="/wiki/Dorset_(unitary_authority)" title="Dorset (unitary authority)">Dorset</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> The two new authorities will come into being on 1 April 2019.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Representation">National Representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: National Representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Parliamentary_constituencies_in_Dorset" title="List of Parliamentary constituencies in Dorset">List of Parliamentary constituencies in Dorset</a></div>\n<p>For representation in <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">Parliament</a> Dorset is divided into eight Parliamentary constituencies\xe2\x80\x94five <a href="/wiki/County_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="County constituencies">county constituencies</a> and three <a href="/wiki/Borough_constituencies" class="mw-redirect" title="Borough constituencies">borough constituencies</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2017" title="United Kingdom general election, 2017">2017 general election</a>, the Conservative Party was dominant, taking all eight seats.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The borough constituencies of <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_East_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bournemouth East (UK Parliament constituency)">Bournemouth East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_West_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Bournemouth West (UK Parliament constituency)">Bournemouth West</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poole_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Poole (UK Parliament constituency)">Poole</a> are traditionally Conservative <a href="/wiki/Safe_seat" title="Safe seat">safe seats</a> and are all represented by Conservative members of parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2017DS_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2017DS-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The county constituencies of <a href="/wiki/North_Dorset_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="North Dorset (UK Parliament constituency)">North Dorset</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Christchurch (UK Parliament constituency)">Christchurch</a> are also represented by Conservative MPs. <a href="/wiki/West_Dorset_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="West Dorset (UK Parliament constituency)">West Dorset</a> is represented by Conservative MP <a href="/wiki/Oliver_Letwin" title="Oliver Letwin">Oliver Letwin</a> who was the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_Office" title="Cabinet Office">Minister of State at the Cabinet Office</a> in David Cameron\'s government.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2017DW_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2017DW-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The marginal seat of <a href="/wiki/South_Dorset_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="South Dorset (UK Parliament constituency)">South Dorset</a> is represented by <a href="/wiki/Richard_Drax" title="Richard Drax">Richard Drax</a>, who gained the seat from Labour representative, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Knight" title="Jim Knight">Jim Knight</a>, in 2010. Drax retained the seat in 2015 and 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_Knight_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_Knight-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2017DS_135-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2017DS-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Mid_Dorset_and_North_Poole_(UK_Parliament_constituency)" title="Mid Dorset and North Poole (UK Parliament constituency)">Mid Dorset and North Poole</a> constituency has been represented by the Conservative MP, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Tomlinson" title="Michael Tomlinson">Michael Tomlinson</a> since 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-2017MP_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2017MP-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> For the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">European Parliament</a> the county lies within the <a href="/wiki/South_West_England_(European_Parliament_constituency)" title="South West England (European Parliament constituency)">South West England</a> constituency which elected two Conservative, two <a href="/wiki/UKIP" class="mw-redirect" title="UKIP">UKIP</a>, one Labour and one Green Party <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_European_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Members of the European Parliament">Members of the European Parliament</a> (MEPs) at the <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament_election,_2014_(United_Kingdom)" title="European Parliament election, 2014 (United Kingdom)">2014 European Parliament election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_industry">Economy and industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy and industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable floatright" style="text-align:center; font-size:95%;" width="40%">\n<caption>Dorset\'s employment structure (2008)<sup class="reference" id="ref_excludes^"><a href="#endnote_excludes^">[A]</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">Industry\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Dorset<sup class="reference" id="ref_excluding^"><a href="#endnote_excluding^">[C]</a></sup><br /><sup id="cite_ref-Dorstnomis_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorstnomis-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Poole<br /><sup id="cite_ref-Poolenomis_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Poolenomis-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Bournemouth<br /><sup id="cite_ref-Bmthnomis_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bmthnomis-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Great Britain<br /><sup id="cite_ref-Dorstnomis_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorstnomis-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Manufacturing\n</th>\n<td>11.9%</td>\n<td>15.8%</td>\n<td>3.2%</td>\n<td>10.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Construction\n</th>\n<td>5.3%</td>\n<td>4.6%</td>\n<td>3.2%</td>\n<td>4.8%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Services\n</th>\n<td>81.5%</td>\n<td>79%</td>\n<td>93.1%</td>\n<td>83.5%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<th scope="row">Tourism-related<sup class="reference" id="ref_includes^"><a href="#endnote_includes^">[B]</a></sup>\n</th>\n<td>10.2%</td>\n<td>7.7%</td>\n<td>12%</td>\n<td>8.2%\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td align="left" colspan="30" style="font-size: 8pt">\n<p>A.<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_excludes^"><a href="#ref_excludes^"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Excludes <a href="/wiki/Self-employed" class="mw-redirect" title="Self-employed">self-employed</a>, government-supported trainees and <a href="/wiki/British_Armed_Forces" title="British Armed Forces">armed forces</a><br />\nB.<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_includes^"><a href="#ref_includes^"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Includes industries that are also part of the services industry<br />\nC.<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_excluding^"><a href="#ref_excluding^"><b><sup>^</sup></b></a></span> Excluding Poole and Bournemouth\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In 2003 the <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">gross value added</a> (GVA) for the non-metropolitan county was \xc2\xa34,673&#160;million, with an additional \xc2\xa34,705&#160;million for Poole and Bournemouth.<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_p249_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA_p249-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Primary_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Primary industry">Primary industry</a> produced 2.03% of GVA, <a href="/wiki/Secondary_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Secondary industry">secondary industry</a> produced 22.44% and 75.53% came from <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Tertiary industry">tertiary industry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_p249_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA_p249-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The average GVA for the 16 regions of <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West England</a> was \xc2\xa34,693&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_p249_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA_p249-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The principal industry in Dorset was once agriculture. It has not, however, been the largest employer since the mid 19th century as <a href="/wiki/Mechanisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Mechanisation">mechanisation</a> substantially reduced the number of workers required.<sup id="cite_ref-Draper105,143_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draper105,143-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Agriculture has become less profitable and the industry has declined further. Within the administrative county between 1995 and 2003, GVA for primary industry (largely agriculture, fishing and quarrying) declined from \xc2\xa3229&#160;million to \xc2\xa3188&#160;million\xe2\x80\x947.1% to 4.0%.<sup id="cite_ref-GVA_p249_145-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GVA_p249-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, 2,039&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (787&#160;sq&#160;mi) of the county was in agricultural use, up from 1,986&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (767&#160;sq&#160;mi) in 1989, although this was due to an increase in permanent grass, and land <a href="/wiki/Set_aside" class="mw-redirect" title="Set aside">set aside</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_farmland_use_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_farmland_use-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> By contrast, in the same period, <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a> decreased from 9,925 to 9,157&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (3,832 to 3,536&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_farmland_use_148-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_farmland_use-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Excluding fowl, sheep are the most common animal stock in the county; between 1989 and 2006 their numbers fell from 252,189 to 193,500. Cattle and pig farming has declined similarly; during the same period the number of cattle fell from 240,413 to 170,700, and pigs from 169,636 to 72,700.<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_Livestock_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_Livestock-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009 there were 2,340 armed forces personnel stationed in Dorset including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Armoured_Corps" title="Royal Armoured Corps">Royal Armoured Corps</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bovington_Camp" title="Bovington Camp">Bovington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Corps_of_Signals" title="Royal Corps of Signals">Royal Signals</a> at <a href="/wiki/Blandford_Camp" title="Blandford Camp">Blandford</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a> at <a href="/wiki/RM_Poole" title="RM Poole">Poole</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The military presence has had a mixed effect on the local economy, bringing additional employment for civilians, but on occasion having a negative impact on the tourist trade, particularly when popular areas are closed for military manoeuvres.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Plans to relocate the <a href="/wiki/Royal_School_of_Signals" title="Royal School of Signals">Royal School of Signals</a> from Blandford to South Wales could result in a loss of up to \xc2\xa374&#160;million GVA for the area.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other major employers in the county include: <a href="/wiki/BAE_Systems" title="BAE Systems">BAE Systems</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sunseeker_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunseeker International">Sunseeker International</a>, <a href="/wiki/J.P._Morgan_Chase" class="mw-redirect" title="J.P. Morgan Chase">J.P. Morgan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cobham_plc" title="Cobham plc">Cobham plc</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_University" title="Bournemouth University">Bournemouth University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Dorset\'s three ports, <a href="/wiki/Poole_Harbour" title="Poole Harbour">Poole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_Harbour,_Dorset" title="Weymouth Harbour, Dorset">Weymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portland_Harbour" title="Portland Harbour">Portland</a>, and the smaller harbours of Christchurch, Swanage, Lyme Regis, Wareham and West Bay generate a substantial amount of international trade and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-Coastal_Economy_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coastal_Economy-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Around 230 fishing vessels that predominantly catch crab and lobster are based in Dorset\'s ports.<sup id="cite_ref-Fishing_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fishing-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> When the waters around Weymouth and Portland were chosen for the sailing events in the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympic Games</a>, the area underwent an increased investment in infrastructure and a growth in the marine leisure sector. It is expected that this will continue to have a positive effect on local businesses and tourism.<sup id="cite_ref-W&amp;P_Strategy_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-W&amp;P_Strategy-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bournemouth_07.JPG" class="image"><img alt="photograph of a crowded Bournemouth beach, near Bournemouth pier, on a hot summer&#39;s day" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Bournemouth_07.JPG/260px-Bournemouth_07.JPG" width="260" height="134" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Bournemouth_07.JPG/390px-Bournemouth_07.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Bournemouth_07.JPG/520px-Bournemouth_07.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1058" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bournemouth_07.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The beach near <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Pier" class="mw-redirect" title="Bournemouth Pier">Bournemouth Pier</a>. Dorset\'s coastline is a major attraction for tourists.</div></div></div>\n<p>Tourism has grown in Dorset since the late 18th century and is now the predominant industry.<sup id="cite_ref-DCF_Tourism_p1_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCF_Tourism_p1-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> It is estimated that 37,500 people work in Dorset\'s tourism sector.<sup id="cite_ref-DCF_Tourism_p3_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCF_Tourism_p3-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> Some 3.2&#160;million British and 326,000 foreign tourists visited the county in 2008, staying a total of 15.1 million nights.<sup id="cite_ref-VOT_2008_p1_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOT_2008_p1-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> In addition there were 14.6&#160;million day visitors.<sup id="cite_ref-VOT_2008_p1_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOT_2008_p1-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The combined spending of both groups was \xc2\xa31,458&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-VOT_2008_p1_160-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOT_2008_p1-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Towns received 56% of Dorset\'s day trippers, 27% went to the coast and 17% to the countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-VOT_2008_p7_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VOT_2008_p7-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> A survey carried out in 1997 concluded that the primary reason tourists were drawn to Dorset was the attractiveness of the county\'s coast and countryside.<sup id="cite_ref-DCF_Tourism_p4_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCF_Tourism_p4-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> Numbers of domestic and foreign tourists have fluctuated in recent years due to various factors including security and economic downturn, a trend reflected throughout the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-uktourismdecline_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uktourismdecline-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Manufacturing industry in Dorset provided 10.3% of employment in 2008. This was slightly above the average for Great Britain but below that of the South West region which was at 10.7% for that period.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The sector is the county\'s fourth largest employer, but a predicted decline suggests there will be 10,200 fewer jobs in manufacturing by 2026.<sup id="cite_ref-Grimley_p78_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grimley_p78-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Dorset" title="Culture of Dorset">Culture of Dorset</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Keep_Military_Museum,_Dorchester,_Dorset-16Sept2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="photograph of The Keep Military Museum in Dorchester" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Keep_Military_Museum%2C_Dorchester%2C_Dorset-16Sept2009.jpg/170px-The_Keep_Military_Museum%2C_Dorchester%2C_Dorset-16Sept2009.jpg" width="170" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Keep_Military_Museum%2C_Dorchester%2C_Dorset-16Sept2009.jpg/255px-The_Keep_Military_Museum%2C_Dorchester%2C_Dorset-16Sept2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/The_Keep_Military_Museum%2C_Dorchester%2C_Dorset-16Sept2009.jpg/340px-The_Keep_Military_Museum%2C_Dorchester%2C_Dorset-16Sept2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2976" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Keep_Military_Museum,_Dorchester,_Dorset-16Sept2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/The_Keep,_Dorchester" title="The Keep, Dorchester">The Keep Military Museum</a> in Dorchester</div></div></div>\n<p>As a largely rural county, Dorset has fewer major cultural institutions than larger or more densely populated areas. Major venues for concerts and theatre include Poole\'s <a href="/wiki/The_Lighthouse_(Poole)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Lighthouse (Poole)">Lighthouse</a> arts centre, Bournemouth\'s <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_International_Centre" title="Bournemouth International Centre">BIC</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pavilion_Theatre_(Bournemouth)" title="Pavilion Theatre (Bournemouth)">Pavilion Theatre</a> and <a href="/wiki/O2_Academy_Bournemouth" title="O2 Academy Bournemouth">O2 Academy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_Pavilion" title="Weymouth Pavilion">Pavilion</a> theatre in Weymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_theatres_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_theatres-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> One of Dorset\'s most noted cultural institutions is the <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Bournemouth Symphony Orchestra">Bournemouth Symphony Orchestra</a> which was founded in 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_Cultstrat_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_Cultstrat-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bso_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bso-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Based in Poole, the orchestra performs over 130 concerts across southern England each year.<sup id="cite_ref-bso_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bso-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorset has more than 30 general and specialist museums.<sup id="cite_ref-DFY_museums_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DFY_museums-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Find_a_museum_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Find_a_museum-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dorset_County_Museum" title="Dorset County Museum">Dorset County Museum</a> in Dorchester was founded in 1846 and contains an extensive collection of exhibits covering the county\'s history and environment.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Tank_Museum" title="The Tank Museum">The Tank Museum</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bovington" class="mw-redirect" title="Bovington">Bovington</a> contains more than 300 tanks and armoured vehicles from 30 nations.<sup id="cite_ref-culture24_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture24-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The museum is the largest in Dorset and its collection has been <a href="/wiki/Designation_Scheme" title="Designation Scheme">designated of national importance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-culture24_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-culture24-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> Other museums which reflect the cultural heritage of the county include <a href="/wiki/The_Keep,_Dorchester" title="The Keep, Dorchester">The Keep Military Museum</a> in Dorchester, the <a href="/wiki/Russell-Cotes_Museum" class="mw-redirect" title="Russell-Cotes Museum">Russell-Cotes Museum</a> in Bournemouth, the <a href="/wiki/Charmouth_Heritage_Coast_Centre" title="Charmouth Heritage Coast Centre">Charmouth Heritage Coast Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poole_Museum" title="Poole Museum">Poole Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portland_Museum,_Dorset" title="Portland Museum, Dorset">Portland Museum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wareham_Town_Museum" title="Wareham Town Museum">Wareham Town Museum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Find_a_museum_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Find_a_museum-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DSP_CultStrat_p15_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DSP_CultStrat_p15-176">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorset contains 190 <a href="/wiki/Conservation_area_(United_Kingdom)" title="Conservation area (United Kingdom)">conservation areas</a>, more than 1,500 <a href="/wiki/Scheduled_monument" title="Scheduled monument">scheduled monuments</a>, over 30 registered parks and gardens and 12,850 <a href="/wiki/Listed_building" title="Listed building">listed buildings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Grade I listed buildings include: <a href="/wiki/Portland_Castle" title="Portland Castle">Portland Castle</a>, a coastal fort commissioned by <a href="/wiki/Henry_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Henry VIII">Henry VIII</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Corfe_Castle" title="Corfe Castle">castle</a> with more than a 1,000 years of history at <a href="/wiki/Corfe_Castle" title="Corfe Castle">Corfe</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Town_House,_Dorchester" title="Roman Town House, Dorchester">Roman ruin</a> described by <a href="/wiki/English_Heritage" title="English Heritage">English Heritage</a> as the "only Roman town house visible in Britain";<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Athelhampton" title="Athelhampton">Athelhampton</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Tudor_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Tudor dynasty">Tudor</a> manor house;<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Forde_Abbey" title="Forde Abbey">Forde Abbey</a>, a stately home and former <a href="/wiki/Cistercian" class="mw-redirect" title="Cistercian">Cistercian</a> monastery;<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Priory" title="Christchurch Priory">Christchurch Priory</a>, the longest church in England;<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/St_Edwold%27s_Church,_Stockwood" title="St Edwold&#39;s Church, Stockwood">St Edwold\'s church</a>, one of the smallest.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steam_Up_-_geograph.org.uk_-_187885.jpg" class="image"><img alt="photograph of a row of traction engines at the Great Dorset Steam Fair" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Steam_Up_-_geograph.org.uk_-_187885.jpg/220px-Steam_Up_-_geograph.org.uk_-_187885.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Steam_Up_-_geograph.org.uk_-_187885.jpg/330px-Steam_Up_-_geograph.org.uk_-_187885.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Steam_Up_-_geograph.org.uk_-_187885.jpg/440px-Steam_Up_-_geograph.org.uk_-_187885.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steam_Up_-_geograph.org.uk_-_187885.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Traction_engine" title="Traction engine">Traction engines</a> on display at the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dorset_Steam_Fair" title="Great Dorset Steam Fair">Great Dorset Steam Fair</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Dorset hosts a number of annual festivals, fairs and events including the <a href="/wiki/Great_Dorset_Steam_Fair" title="Great Dorset Steam Fair">Great Dorset Steam Fair</a> near Blandford, one of the largest events of its kind in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Air_Festival" title="Bournemouth Air Festival">Bournemouth Air Festival</a>, a free <a href="/wiki/Air_show" title="Air show">air show</a> that attracted 1.3&#160;million visitors in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> The Spirit of the Seas is a maritime festival held in Weymouth and Portland. Launched in 2008, the festival features sporting activities, cultural events and local entertainers.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The Dorset County Show, which was first held in 1841, is a celebration of Dorset\'s agriculture.<sup id="cite_ref-DCS_BBC_News_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCS_BBC_News-189">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> The two-day event exhibits local produce and livestock and attracts some 55,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-DCS_BBC_News_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCS_BBC_News-189">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> Inside Out Dorset is an outdoor arts festival produced by <a href="/wiki/Dorchester,_Dorset" title="Dorchester, Dorset">Dorchester</a>-based Activate Performing Arts that takes place every two years in rural and urban locations across Dorset.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the smaller folk festivals held in towns such as Christchurch and <a href="/wiki/Wimborne_Folk_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Wimborne Folk Festival">Wimborne</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> Dorset holds several larger musical events such as <a href="/wiki/Camp_Bestival" title="Camp Bestival">Camp Bestival</a>, <a href="/wiki/End_Of_The_Road_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="End Of The Road Festival">End of the Road</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Larmer_Tree_Festival" title="Larmer Tree Festival">Larmer Tree Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorset\'s only professional football club is <a href="/wiki/A.F.C._Bournemouth" title="A.F.C. Bournemouth">A.F.C. Bournemouth</a>, which plays in <a href="/wiki/The_Premier_League" class="mw-redirect" title="The Premier League">the Premier League</a>\xe2\x80\x94 the highest division in the <a href="/wiki/English_football_league_system" title="English football league system">English football league system</a>. <a href="/wiki/Non-League_football" title="Non-League football">Non-League</a> semi-professional teams in the county include <a href="/wiki/Southern_Football_League" title="Southern Football League">Southern Premier Division</a> teams <a href="/wiki/Dorchester_Town_F.C." title="Dorchester Town F.C.">Dorchester Town F.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poole_Town_F.C." title="Poole Town F.C.">Poole Town F.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_F.C." title="Weymouth F.C.">Weymouth F.C.</a>. <a href="/wiki/Dorset_County_Cricket_Club" title="Dorset County Cricket Club">Dorset County Cricket Club</a> competes in the <a href="/wiki/Minor_Counties_Cricket_Championship" title="Minor Counties Cricket Championship">Minor Counties Cricket Championship</a> and is based at <a href="/wiki/Dean_Park_Cricket_Ground" title="Dean Park Cricket Ground">Dean Park Cricket Ground</a> in Bournemouth. <a href="/wiki/Poole_Stadium" title="Poole Stadium">Poole Stadium</a> hosts regular greyhound racing and is the home to top-flight speedway team <a href="/wiki/Poole_Pirates" title="Poole Pirates">Poole Pirates</a>. The county\'s coastline, on the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a>, is noted for its watersports (particularly sailing, <a href="/wiki/Gig_racing" class="mw-redirect" title="Gig racing">gig racing</a>, windsurfing, power boating and kayaking) which take advantage of the sheltered waters in the bays of <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_Bay" title="Weymouth Bay">Weymouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poole_Bay" title="Poole Bay">Poole</a>, and the harbours of Poole and Portland.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-weymouthwatersports_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-weymouthwatersports-198">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-poolewatersports_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poolewatersports-199">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> Dorset hosted the sailing events at the 2012 Summer Olympics and 2012 Summer Paralympics at the <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_and_Portland_National_Sailing_Academy" title="Weymouth and Portland National Sailing Academy">Weymouth and Portland National Sailing Academy</a>.   The venue was completed in May 2009 and was used by international sailing teams in preparation for the Games.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomashardy_restored.jpg" class="image"><img alt="photograph of the author, Thomas Hardy, taken circa 1910" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Thomashardy_restored.jpg/170px-Thomashardy_restored.jpg" width="170" height="247" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Thomashardy_restored.jpg/255px-Thomashardy_restored.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Thomashardy_restored.jpg/340px-Thomashardy_restored.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3663" data-file-height="5316" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Thomashardy_restored.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hardy" title="Thomas Hardy">Thomas Hardy</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Dorset is famed in literature for being the native county of author and poet <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hardy" title="Thomas Hardy">Thomas Hardy</a>, and many of the places he describes in his novels in the fictional <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hardy%27s_Wessex" title="Thomas Hardy&#39;s Wessex">Wessex</a> are in Dorset, which he renamed <i>South Wessex</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Dorset&#39;s_writers_BBC_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorset&#39;s_writers_BBC-204">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Places_of_Historic_Interest_or_Natural_Beauty" title="National Trust for Places of Historic Interest or Natural Beauty">National Trust</a> owns <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hardy%27s_Cottage" title="Thomas Hardy&#39;s Cottage">Thomas Hardy\'s Cottage</a>, in Higher Bockhampton, east of Dorchester; and <a href="/wiki/Max_Gate" title="Max Gate">Max Gate</a>, his former house in Dorchester.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Several other writers have called Dorset home, including <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Adams" title="Douglas Adams">Douglas Adams</a>, who wrote much of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hitchhiker%27s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy" title="The Hitchhiker&#39;s Guide to the Galaxy">The Hitchhiker\'s Guide to the Galaxy</a></i> while he lived in <a href="/wiki/Stalbridge" title="Stalbridge">Stalbridge</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_le_Carr%C3%A9" title="John le Carr\xc3\xa9">John le Carr\xc3\xa9</a>, author of espionage novels, was born in Poole;<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tom_Sharpe" title="Tom Sharpe">Tom Sharpe</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Wilt_(novel)" title="Wilt (novel)">Wilt</a></i> fame lived in Bridport;<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Fowles" title="John Fowles">John Fowles</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_French_Lieutenant%27s_Woman" title="The French Lieutenant&#39;s Woman">The French Lieutenant\'s Woman</a></i>) lived in Lyme Regis before he died in late 2005;<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/T.F._Powys" class="mw-redirect" title="T.F. Powys">T.F. Powys</a> lived in <a href="/wiki/Chaldon_Herring" title="Chaldon Herring">Chaldon Herring</a> for over 20 years and used it as inspiration for the fictitious village of Folly Down in his novel <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Weston%27s_Good_Wine" class="mw-redirect" title="Mr. Weston&#39;s Good Wine">Mr. Weston\'s Good Wine</a></i>;<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/John_Cowper_Powys" title="John Cowper Powys">John Cowper Powys</a>, his elder brother, also set a number of his works in Dorset, such as the novels <i><a href="/wiki/Maiden_Castle_(novel)" title="Maiden Castle (novel)">Maiden Castle</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Weymouth_Sands" title="Weymouth Sands">Weymouth Sands</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> The 19th-century poet <a href="/wiki/William_Barnes" title="William Barnes">William Barnes</a> was born in <a href="/wiki/Bagber" title="Bagber">Bagber</a> and wrote many poems in his native <a href="/wiki/West_Country_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="West Country dialect">Dorset dialect</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dorset&#39;s_writers_BBC_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorset&#39;s_writers_BBC-204">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Originating from the ancient <a href="/wiki/Proto-Norse_language" title="Proto-Norse language">Norse</a> and <a href="/wiki/Old_Saxon" title="Old Saxon">Saxon</a> languages, the dialect was prevalent across the Blackmore Vale but has fallen into disuse.<sup id="cite_ref-Dorset_Echo_4.5.11_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dorset_Echo_4.5.11-213">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Dorset" title="Flag of Dorset">Dorset\'s flag</a>, which is known as the Dorset Cross or St Wite\'s Cross, was adopted in 2008 following a public competition organised by Dorset County Council.<sup id="cite_ref-FRUK_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FRUK-215">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> The winning design, which features a white cross with a red border on a golden background, attracted 54% of the vote.<sup id="cite_ref-flag_bbc_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flag_bbc-217">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> All three colours are used in Dorset County Council\'s coat of arms and the red and white was used in recognition of the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_England" title="Flag of England">English flag</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-flag_explained_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flag_explained-218">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The golden colour represents Dorset\'s sandy beaches and the Dorset landmarks of <a href="/wiki/Golden_Cap" title="Golden Cap">Golden Cap</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gold_Hill,_Shaftesbury" title="Gold Hill, Shaftesbury">Gold Hill</a>. It is also a reference to the <a href="/wiki/Wessex#Wyvern_or_dragon" title="Wessex">Wessex Dragon</a>, a symbol of the <a href="/wiki/Wessex" title="Wessex">Saxon Kingdom</a> which Dorset once belonged to, and the gold wreath featured on the badge of the <a href="/wiki/Dorset_Regiment" title="Dorset Regiment">Dorset Regiment</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-flag_explained_218-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-flag_explained-218">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Dorset" title="Transport in Dorset">Transport in Dorset</a></div>\n<p>Dorset is connected to London by two main line railways. The <a href="/wiki/West_of_England_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="West of England Main Line">West of England Main Line</a> runs through the north of the county at Gillingham and Sherborne.<sup id="cite_ref-Route_4_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Route_4-219">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> Running west from <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_station" title="London Waterloo station">London Waterloo</a> to <a href="/wiki/Exeter_St_Davids_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Exeter St Davids railway station">Exeter St Davids</a> in Devon, it provides a service for those who live in the western districts of Dorset.<sup id="cite_ref-Route_4_219-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Route_4-219">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/South_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="South Western Main Line">South Western Main Line</a> runs through the south at Bournemouth, Poole, Dorchester and the terminus at Weymouth.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Additionally, the <a href="/wiki/Heart_of_Wessex_Line" title="Heart of Wessex Line">Heart of Wessex Line</a> runs north from Weymouth to <a href="/wiki/Bristol" title="Bristol">Bristol</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Swanage_Railway" title="Swanage Railway">Swanage Railway</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Heritage_railway" title="Heritage railway">heritage steam and diesel railway</a>, runs the 10 kilometres (6&#160;mi) between <a href="/wiki/Norden_railway_station_(Dorset)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norden railway station (Dorset)">Norden</a> and Swanage.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorset is one of the few counties in England not to have a motorway.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/A303_road" title="A303 road">A303</a>, <a href="/wiki/A35_road" title="A35 road">A35</a> and <a href="/wiki/A31_road" title="A31 road">A31</a> <a href="/wiki/Trunk_road" title="Trunk road">trunk roads</a> run through the county.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> The A303, which connects the <a href="/wiki/West_Country" title="West Country">West Country</a> to London via the <a href="/wiki/M3_motorway_(Great_Britain)" title="M3 motorway (Great Britain)">M3</a>, clips the north-west of the county.<sup id="cite_ref-googlemapdorset_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-googlemapdorset-224">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The A35 crosses the county in a west-east direction from <a href="/wiki/Honiton" title="Honiton">Honiton</a> in Devon, via Bridport, Dorchester, Poole, Bournemouth and Christchurch, to <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">Southampton</a> in Hampshire. The A31 connects to the A35 at <a href="/wiki/Bere_Regis" title="Bere Regis">Bere Regis</a>, and passes east through Wimborne and Ferndown to Hampshire, where it later becomes the <a href="/wiki/M27_motorway_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="M27 motorway (England)">M27</a>. Other main roads in the county include the <a href="/wiki/A338" class="mw-redirect" title="A338">A338</a>, <a href="/wiki/A354" class="mw-redirect" title="A354">A354</a>, <a href="/wiki/A37_road_(England)" class="mw-redirect" title="A37 road (England)">A37</a> and <a href="/wiki/A350_road" title="A350 road">A350</a>. The A338 heads north from Bournemouth to <a href="/wiki/Ringwood" title="Ringwood">Ringwood</a> (Hampshire) and on to <a href="/wiki/Salisbury" title="Salisbury">Salisbury</a> (Wiltshire) and beyond. The A354 also connects to Salisbury after travelling north-east from Weymouth in the south of the county. The A37 travels north-west from Dorchester to <a href="/wiki/Yeovil" title="Yeovil">Yeovil</a> in Somerset. The A350 also leads north, from Poole through <a href="/wiki/Blandford" class="mw-redirect" title="Blandford">Blandford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shaftesbury" title="Shaftesbury">Shaftesbury</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Warminster" title="Warminster">Warminster</a> in Wiltshire.<sup id="cite_ref-googlemapdorset_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-googlemapdorset-224">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Two passenger sea ports and an international airport are situated in the county. <a href="/wiki/Brittany_Ferries" title="Brittany Ferries">Brittany Ferries</a> and <a href="/wiki/Condor_Ferries" title="Condor Ferries">Condor Ferries</a>, operate out of Poole Harbour; Brittany Ferries provide access to <a href="/wiki/Cherbourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Cherbourg">Cherbourg</a> in France and Condor Ferries sail a seasonal service to the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Malo" class="mw-redirect" title="St Malo">St Malo</a>, France.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Condor Ferries operated services from Weymouth harbour to Guernsey, Jersey and St. Malo throughout the year however, these ceased in 2015.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.bbc.co.uk/news/uk-england-dorset-32013883">[1]</a><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> Poole, since the dredging of the main channel in 2008, and Portland harbours are capable of taking cruise liners.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_Airport" title="Bournemouth Airport">Bournemouth Airport</a>, which is situated on the edge of <a href="/wiki/Hurn" title="Hurn">Hurn</a> village 6 kilometres (4&#160;mi) north of Bournemouth, has flights to 36 destinations and serves some 600,000 passengers a year.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> In August 2007 work began on a \xc2\xa332&#160;million expansion programme which includes enlargement of the terminal building and an increase in parking.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorset is served by 14 commercial bus operators.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Go_South_Coast" title="Go South Coast">morebus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Go_South_Coast" title="Go South Coast">Damory</a> share a county wide network with frequent services linking major towns, including Bournemouth, Poole and Wimborne, and a varied service in further rural locations.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/First_Hampshire_%26_Dorset" title="First Hampshire &amp; Dorset">First Group</a> operate buses in the Weymouth and Bridport area, including: a regular route along the A35 from Weymouth to Axminster, which helps to compensate for the missing rail link west of Dorchester; and the Jurassic Coast service, one of the longest bus routes in the UK, which provides through travel from Poole to Exeter, exploiting a popular tourist route.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Buses" title="Yellow Buses">Yellow Buses</a> provide some bus services within Bournemouth and outlying areas.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_sites">Religious sites</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religious sites">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_monastic_houses_in_Dorset" title="List of monastic houses in Dorset">List of monastic houses in Dorset</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sherborne_Abbey_-_2639839.jpg" class="image"><img alt="the exterior of Sherborne Abbey" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Sherborne_Abbey_-_2639839.jpg/220px-Sherborne_Abbey_-_2639839.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Sherborne_Abbey_-_2639839.jpg/330px-Sherborne_Abbey_-_2639839.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Sherborne_Abbey_-_2639839.jpg/440px-Sherborne_Abbey_-_2639839.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sherborne_Abbey_-_2639839.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sherborne_Abbey" title="Sherborne Abbey">Sherborne Abbey</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Unlike all of its neighbouring counties, Dorset does not have a cathedral.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> Over 95% of the county falls within the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Salisbury" title="Diocese of Salisbury">Diocese of Salisbury</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> A small section to the west comes under the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Bath_and_Wells" title="Diocese of Bath and Wells">Diocese of Bath and Wells</a> and to the east Christchurch and much of Bournemouth\xe2\x80\x94both historically part of Hampshire\xe2\x80\x94belong to the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Winchester" title="Diocese of Winchester">Diocese of Winchester</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Plymouth" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Plymouth">Roman Catholic Diocese of Plymouth</a> incorporates most of Dorset with the exception of Christchurch and a portion of Bournemouth which belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Portsmouth" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Portsmouth">Diocese of Portsmouth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> Few purpose-built places of worship exist in Dorset for faiths other than Christianity. In 2008 a Hindu temple was constructed in Blandford Forum for the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Gurkha_Signals" title="Queen&#39;s Gurkha Signals">Gurkhas</a> based at the town\'s military camp. Bournemouth, which contains a higher proportion of Jewish residents than the national average, has two synagogues.<sup id="cite_ref-ONS_Bournemouth_religion_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ONS_Bournemouth_religion-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christianity was introduced to Dorset by the Romans.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> A 4th century <a href="/wiki/Hinton_St_Mary_Mosaic" title="Hinton St Mary Mosaic">Roman mosaic</a> discovered near <a href="/wiki/Hinton_St_Mary" title="Hinton St Mary">Hinton St Mary</a> contains what is generally accepted to be an image of Christ.<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> Christianity became firmly established in the county during the Saxon period although there are few surviving Saxon churches; the most complete is <a href="/wiki/St_Martin%27s_Church,_Wareham" title="St Martin&#39;s Church, Wareham">St. Martin\'s</a> in Wareham which has features from the early 11th century.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Mediaeval churches are more prevalent in Dorset; most are 15th century and are of a <a href="/wiki/Perpendicular_Gothic" class="mw-redirect" title="Perpendicular Gothic">Perpendicular</a> style.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sherborne_Abbey" title="Sherborne Abbey">Sherborne Abbey</a>, one of the county\'s largest, is noted for its broad <a href="/wiki/Fan_vault" title="Fan vault">fan vaulting</a> added during an extensive 15th century rebuild.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup> Founded in AD&#160;705 by <a href="/wiki/Aldhelm" title="Aldhelm">Aldhelm</a>, the Abbey contained the <a href="/wiki/Cathedra" title="Cathedra">chair</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Sherborne" title="Bishop of Sherborne">Bishop of Sherborne</a> and was granted cathedral status until 1075 when the diocese was transferred to <a href="/wiki/Old_Sarum" title="Old Sarum">Old Sarum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wimborne_Minster_(church)" title="Wimborne Minster (church)">Wimborne Minster</a> features a <a href="/wiki/Chained_library" title="Chained library">chained library</a> and a 14th-century <a href="/wiki/Astronomical_clock" title="Astronomical clock">astronomical clock</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Priory" title="Christchurch Priory">Christchurch Priory</a> is renowned for its <a href="/wiki/Christchurch_Priory#Miraculous_beam" title="Christchurch Priory">miraculous beam</a> which, according to legend, was installed by Christ;<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup> and the 15th century roof spanning the <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">nave</a> at St John the Baptist Church in Bere Regis is described by architectural historian <a href="/wiki/Nikolaus_Pevsner" title="Nikolaus Pevsner">Nikolaus Pevsner</a> as the "finest timber roof of Dorset".<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Church_of_St_Candida_and_Holy_Cross" title="Church of St Candida and Holy Cross">St Candida and Holy Cross</a> at <a href="/wiki/Whitchurch_Canonicorum" title="Whitchurch Canonicorum">Whitchurch Canonicorum</a> is the only church in the country, besides <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a>, to have a shrine that contains the <a href="/wiki/Relic" title="Relic">relics</a> of a saint.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Monastic foundations were once abundant in Dorset, but all ceased to exist at the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_monasteries" class="mw-redirect" title="Dissolution of the monasteries">Dissolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">Reformation</a> and the political and religious turmoil that ensued largely checked the building of new churches until the turn of the 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-JD82_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JD82-256">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Notable examples of <a href="/wiki/Georgian_architecture" title="Georgian architecture">Early Georgian</a> churches include the <a href="/wiki/Bastard_brothers" title="Bastard brothers">Bastard brothers</a>\' Church of St. Peter and St. Paul in Blandford Forum, and <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Church,_Portland" title="St George&#39;s Church, Portland">St George\'s Church</a> on the Isle of Portland, which has a steeple and tower inspired by the works of <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Wren" title="Christopher Wren">Christopher Wren</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> From the late 18th century onwards, churches in Dorset tended towards a <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival</a> style.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> A notable exception to this trend, however, is the Church of St Mary in <a href="/wiki/East_Lulworth" title="East Lulworth">East Lulworth</a>\xe2\x80\x94the first freestanding Roman Catholic church built in England after the <a href="/wiki/English_Reformation" title="English Reformation">Reformation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lehane59_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lehane59-260">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> George III gave permission to erect the building on the condition that it resembled a garden mausoleum rather than a church. It was completed in 1789.<sup id="cite_ref-JD82_256-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JD82-256">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Lehane59_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lehane59-260">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Bournemouth, founded in 1810, has a wealth of 19th-century churches including <a href="/wiki/St_Peter%27s_Church,_Bournemouth" title="St Peter&#39;s Church, Bournemouth">St Peter\'s</a> and <a href="/wiki/St_Stephen%27s_Church,_Bournemouth" title="St Stephen&#39;s Church, Bournemouth">St Stephen\'s</a>. St Dunstan\'s Church (formerly St Osmund\'s) in Poole is one of a small number of 20th-century churches in Dorset. The final major work of <a href="/wiki/Edward_Schroeder_Prior" title="Edward Schroeder Prior">Edward Schroeder Prior</a>, it is one of the last examples of the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Revival_architecture" title="Byzantine Revival architecture">Neo Byzantine style</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> The Church of St Nicholas and St Magnus in <a href="/wiki/Moreton,_Dorset" title="Moreton, Dorset">Moreton</a> is noted for its elaborate engraved glass windows designed by <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Whistler" title="Laurence Whistler">Laurence Whistler</a>. Severely damaged by a stray German bomb in 1940, the church subsequently underwent extensive renovation and Whistler had replaced every window by 1984.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Dorset" title="List of schools in Dorset">List of schools in Dorset</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Bournemouth" title="List of schools in Bournemouth">List of schools in Bournemouth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_schools_in_Poole" title="List of schools in Poole">List of schools in Poole</a></div>\n<p>Responsibility for <a href="/wiki/State_school" title="State school">state schools</a> in Dorset is divided between three <a href="/wiki/Local_education_authority" title="Local education authority">local education authorities</a>: Dorset County Council, which covers the majority of the county, and Bournemouth and Poole unitary authorities. Most of the Dorset County Council area operates a two-tier <a href="/wiki/Comprehensive_school" title="Comprehensive school">comprehensive system</a> whereby pupils attend a primary school before completing their education at secondary school but Corfe Mullen, Dorchester, Ferndown and <a href="/wiki/West_Moors" title="West Moors">West Moors</a> maintain a <a href="/wiki/Three-tier_education" title="Three-tier education">three-tier system</a> (<a href="/wiki/First_school" title="First school">first</a>, <a href="/wiki/Middle_school" title="Middle school">middle</a> and high school).<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> Bournemouth operates a two-tier system; Poole operates two and three-tier systems.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Poole and Bournemouth are two of a minority of local authorities in England to maintain selective education, each containing two <a href="/wiki/Single-sex_education" title="Single-sex education">single-sex</a> <a href="/wiki/Grammar_school" title="Grammar school">grammar schools</a> which select pupils on the basis of an <a href="/wiki/Eleven-plus" title="Eleven-plus">eleven-plus</a> examination. Some of the county\'s schools are <a href="/wiki/Academy_(English_school)" title="Academy (English school)">academies</a>\xe2\x80\x94self-governing state schools which have become independent of their local education authority and are maintained directly by the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Education" title="Department for Education">Department for Education</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Progress_8_benchmark" title="Progress 8 benchmark">Progress 8 score</a> for schools in the county council area was ranked below average, and 39.6% of pupils gained at least Grade 5 or above in English and maths <a href="/wiki/GCSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GCSE">GCSEs</a> matching the national average of 39.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> Poole recorded an above average Progress 8 score and 54% of pupils achieved Grade 5 or above in English and maths GCSEs.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> Bournemouth was ranked as average and 47.8% of pupils achieved Grade 5 or above in English and maths <a href="/wiki/GCSE" class="mw-redirect" title="GCSE">GCSEs</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Dorset contains a range of privately funded independent schools. Many are <a href="/wiki/Boarding_school" title="Boarding school">boarding schools</a> which also take <a href="/wiki/Day_school" title="Day school">day pupils</a>, such as the co-educational <a href="/wiki/Canford_School" title="Canford School">Canford School</a> which is built around a 19th-century Grade I listed <a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">manor house</a>; <a href="/wiki/St_Mary%27s_School,_Shaftesbury" title="St Mary&#39;s School, Shaftesbury">St Mary\'s</a>, a Catholic girls\' school in Shaftesbury; and <a href="/wiki/Sherborne_School" title="Sherborne School">Sherborne School</a>, a boys school founded in the 16th century.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Four of the county\'s five largest towns contain a <a href="/wiki/Further_education" title="Further education">further education</a> college: <a href="/wiki/Weymouth_College" title="Weymouth College">Weymouth College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingston_Maurward_College" title="Kingston Maurward College">Kingston Maurward College</a> in Dorchester and <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_and_Poole_College" title="Bournemouth and Poole College">Bournemouth and Poole College</a> which is one of the largest in the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> Dorset has two higher education establishments situated in the heart of the county\'s south east conurbation. <a href="/wiki/Bournemouth_University" title="Bournemouth University">Bournemouth University</a> has facilities across Bournemouth and Poole and over 17,000 students.<sup id="cite_ref-BU_history_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BU_history-271">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> Previously named Bournemouth Polytechnic, it was granted university status as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Further_and_Higher_Education_Act_1992" title="Further and Higher Education Act 1992">Further and Higher Education Act 1992</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-BU_history_271-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BU_history-271">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Arts_University_Bournemouth" class="mw-redirect" title="The Arts University Bournemouth">The Arts University Bournemouth</a> is situated between the border of Poole and Bournemouth. It became a higher education institute in 2001 and was given degree-awarding powers in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> It was granted full university status in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Flag_of_Dorset.svg/32px-Flag_of_Dorset.svg.png" width="32" height="19" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Flag_of_Dorset.svg/48px-Flag_of_Dorset.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Flag_of_Dorset.svg/64px-Flag_of_Dorset.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="424" data-file-height="254" /></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Dorset" title="Portal:Dorset">Dorset portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Custos_Rotulorum_of_Dorset" title="Custos Rotulorum of Dorset">Custos Rotulorum of Dorset</a>\xe2\x80\x94list of keepers of the rolls for Dorset</li>\n<li><a Commissioner">Dorset Police and Crime Commissioner</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-118"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-118">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">2013 figures are mid year estimates produced by the ONS. Taking the 2011 census as a starting point, each year, the previous year\'s population is aged by one year, births and deaths are added and removed respectively whilst those leaving the county are subtracted and those moving in are added, each according to age and gender.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-125"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-125">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Alterations to Dorset\'s boundary prior to 1974 have been comparatively minor. In 1844 <a href="/wiki/Stockland,_Devon" title="Stockland, Devon">Stockland</a> was transferred to Devon in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Thorncombe" title="Thorncombe">Thorncombe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holwell,_Dorset" title="Holwell, Dorset">Holwell</a> was gained from Somerset. In 1896 the Somerset villages of <a href="/wiki/Adber" title="Adber">Adber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Goathill" title="Goathill">Goathill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poyntington" title="Poyntington">Poyntington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandford_Orcas" title="Sandford Orcas">Sandford Orcas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Seaborough" title="Seaborough">Seaborough</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trent,_Dorset" title="Trent, Dorset">Trent</a> were added in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Wambrook" title="Wambrook">Wambrook</a> while <a href="/wiki/Chardstock" title="Chardstock">Chardstock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hawkchurch" title="Hawkchurch">Hawkchurch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tytherleigh" title="Tytherleigh">Tytherleigh</a> were ceded to Devon.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dorset&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section:
